About TechCrunch "speakable-summary\"> "font-weight: 400;\"> "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/wework\/\">WeWork<\/a> is on the verge of filing for Chapter 11 bankruptcy in New Jersey, according to sources cited by The <\/span> "https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/wework-plans-to-file-for-bankruptcy-as-early-as-next-week-1fdcb6a5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> "font-weight: 400;\">Wall Street Journal<\/span><\/a> "font-weight: 400;\">.<\/span><\/p>\n If WeWork does indeed file, it shouldn’t come as a shock to close followers of the f "font-weight: 400;\">lexible workspace provider. WeWork warned in August in its "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/08\/08\/wework-goes-from-a-47b-valuation-to-subtantial-doubts-about-its-ability-to-continue-as-a-going-concern\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">second-quarter earnings<\/a> that<\/span> "font-weight: 400;\">\u00a0\u201csubstantial doubt exists about the company\u2019s ability to continue as a going concern.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n "font-weight: 400;\">The company has faced a number of challenges for years as demand for its co-working spaces has steadily declined over time. Those troubles compounded during the COVID pandemic when\u00a0<\/span> "font-weight: 400;\">companies abandoned office space and employees began working remotely. Even as some companies have returned to the office, the appetite for WeWork space didn’t rebound to those pre-pandemic days.<\/span><\/p>\n "font-weight: 400;\">Earlier this month, WeWork missed interest payments to its bondholders, and was granted 30 days to come up with those payments, according to <\/span> "https:\/\/d18rn0p25nwr6d.cloudfront.net\/CIK-0001813756\/75fb45d7-d40d-4f34-95e0-51188ec72bb8.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> "font-weight: 400;\">a securities filing<\/span><\/a> "font-weight: 400;\">. On October 30, WeWork said it had begun discussions with \u201ccertain stakeholders in its capital structure\u201d such as SoftBank and Goldman Sachs about improving its balance sheet as it took steps \u201cto rationalize its real estate footprint.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n "font-weight: 400;\">In August, the 13-year-old company announced a net loss of $397 million for the second quarter on revenue of $877 million. While revenue was up 4% year-over-year, WeWork interim CEO David Tolley noted in a statement at the time: \u201cExcess supply in commercial real estate, increasing competition in flexible space and macroeconomic volatility drove higher member churn and softer demand than we anticipated, resulting in a slight decline in memberships.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n "font-weight: 400;\">The company\u2019s stock was <\/span> "https:\/\/finance.yahoo.com\/quote\/WE\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> "font-weight: 400;\">down over 47% after-hours today<\/span><\/a> "font-weight: 400;\">, trading at just $1.21 and hitting a new 52-week low. This gave the company a market cap of just $121 million, a stark contrast to the $47 billion valuation it reached after raising $1 billion in its SoftBank-led Series H round in January 2019.<\/span><\/p>\n "embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n "wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"0pILKwA92b\"> "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/17\/wework-fires-back-at-competitor-codi-with-cease-and-desist\/\">WeWork fires back at competitor Codi with cease and desist following ‘WeWont’ campaign<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote> "piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n "wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“WeWork fires back at competitor Codi with cease and desist following ‘WeWont’ campaign” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/17\/wework-fires-back-at-competitor-codi-with-cease-and-desist\/embed\/#?secret=vSprtrVfCm#?secret=0pILKwA92b\" data-secret=\"0pILKwA92b\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" WeWork is on the verge of filing for Chapter 11 bankruptcy in New Jersey, according to sources cited by The Wall Street Journal. If WeWork does indeed file, it shouldn’t come as a shock to close followers of the flexible workspace provider. h.com\/2023\/10\/31\/google-and-match-group-reach-settlement-in-app-store-antitrust-case\/","title":{"rendered":"Google and Match Group reach settlement in app store antitrust case"},"content":{"rendered":" "speakable-summary\">Google and Match announced today they’ve reached a settlement in the "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/01\/19\/epic-and-matchs-antitrust-case-against-google-heads-to-jury-trial-on-november-6\/\">antitrust battle Match waged against the tech giant,<\/a> even as the court case continues with Fortnite maker Epic Games. As part of the settlement agreement, Match Group — which owns dating apps Tinder, Hinge, OKCupid, Match.com and others — will be able to implement “ "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/09\/02\/google-will-allow-alternative-payment-systems-for-play-store-in-more-countries\/\">user choice billing<\/a>” by March 31, 2024. This feature allows users to pay with other systems besides Google’s own.<\/p>\n Spotify and Bumble were among the initial testers for the new system, "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/11\/10\/google-play-to-pilot-third-party-billing-in-new-markets-including-u-s-bumble-joins-spotify-as-early-tester\/\">first introduced in November 2022<\/a>. Since then, Spotify’s third-party billing option "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/01\/31\/spotifys-third-party-billing-option-has-now-reached-over-140-global-markets\/\"> rolled out to worldwide markets<\/a> as Google expanded user choice billing to "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/11\/10\/google-play-to-pilot-third-party-billing-in-new-markets-including-u-s-bumble-joins-spotify-as-early-tester\/\">more countries outside the U.S.<\/a><\/p>\n The program, so far, has not allowed third-party app markers that charge users for purchases and subscriptions to do away entirely with the commission Google requires. Instead, it offers a small percentage off the standard 15% to 30% commission. Currently, that discount is 4%, "https:\/\/support.google.com\/googleplay\/android-developer\/answer\/12570971\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">per Google’s help documentation.<\/a> The program is also still a pilot open to all developers globally who are selling apps to users in the supported 35 markets where it’s now available. Google has not said when the program will become globally available.<\/p>\n As part of the agreement, Match Group will not be allowed to only<\/em> offer its own billing system — it will offer its system alongside the existing Google Play billing system. Users will be able to choose which way they want to pay.<\/p>\n In addition, the settlement agreement includes a provision that Google will continue to work with Match Group in other areas where the two companies partner, including in Google Cloud and in the use of Google’s AI technologies, a Google spokesperson said. This suggests that the rift between the two tech companies incurred by the lawsuit could have led to more complicated relationships across other areas of both Google and Match’s business.<\/p>\n Like Apple, Google has long stressed that its commission structure is not only based on its ability to process payments for its customers. Instead, it suggests that the fees help to support the entire Google Play and Android app ecosystem, including hosting, app discovery, developer tools and other resources necessary to create an app business.<\/p>\n But as larger companies like Match and Epic have argued, they don’t need the same resources as other developers. In fact, "https:\/\/www.fortnite.com\/mobile\/android\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as Epic demonstrated<\/a>, they could self-distribute apps and manage their own payments. They believed they should then at least have the option to have a more direct relationship with their paying customers, and Google preventing this was an anti-competitive concern.<\/p>\n “We are pleased to reach a settlement agreement with Match Group,” a Google spokesperson said, in a prepared statement. “This ensures we can continue to provide our shared users the secure, seamless, and high-quality experience people expect from apps on Google Play while maintaining Google\u2019s ability to invest in the Android ecosystem and deliver value across an app\u2019s full lifecycle,” they added.<\/p>\n “Today, the Match plaintiffs and Google informed the court that they have reached a binding term sheet for a settlement of their respective claims against each other in the Match Group, LLC et al vs. Google LLC et al lawsuit. Under the terms, the $40 million placed in escrow will be returned to Match Group and no other amounts will be owed by the Match plaintiffs to Google relating to the claims in the lawsuit for the period ending December 31, 2023,” a Match Group statement added, shared alongside the release of its Q3 earnings results.<\/p>\n Recently, "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/08\/11\/google-pushes-match-for-more-money-in-antitrust-battle-court-filing-states\/\"> Google had pushed Match Group for more money in escrow<\/a>, saying that the $40 million would not be enough to cover the missed payments. (Match had been allowed to escrow funds to cover commissions while the lawsuit was underway.)<\/p>\n Match noted that the parties agreed that by March 31, 2024, its apps will implement Google\u2019s User Choice Billing, reducing its commission payments from 15% and 30% to 11% and 26%, respectively.<\/p>\n “The parties will enter a new partnership agreement that will provide value exchange across their broad relationship, which we expect will essentially offset the additional costs that Match Group brands expect to incur over the three years starting in 2024 associated with the implementation and continued use of User Choice Billing in compliance with Google\u2019s payment policy during that period,” Match Group also said.<\/p>\n In addition to the settlement news, Match Group reported a 9% year-over-year increase in revenue in Q3 to $882 million, with Tinder’s portion up 11% to $509 million.<\/p>\n It’s unclear whether this settlement will prompt Epic Games to also reach an agreement with the tech giant. If it does not, it’s set to go to trial next week to present its arguments.<\/p>\n "embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n "wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"qGcXVnzmF8\"> "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/01\/19\/epic-and-matchs-antitrust-case-against-google-heads-to-jury-trial-on-november-6\/\">Epic and Match’s antitrust case against Google heads to jury trial on November 6<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n "wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; la-wins-fatal-autopilot-crash-jury-trial\/","title":{"rendered":"Tesla wins fatal Autopilot crash jury trial"},"content":{"rendered":" "speakable-summary\">A jury on Tuesday handed Tesla another win after siding with the automaker over allegations that its Autopilot advanced driver assistance system led to a death.<\/p>\n The case, which was being tried in the Superior Court of California, County of Riverside, was filed by two passengers who survived a 2019 crash and alleged that Tesla knew its product was defective. The two survivors sought $400 million in damages for the loss of the driver’s life, physical injury and mental anguish.<\/p>\n Tesla argued that the crash, which resulted in the death of the driver Micah Lee, was the result of human error \u2014 the same stance it’s taken in other Autopilot lawsuits.<\/p>\n While Tesla has won other lawsuits, including a California jury trial earlier this year that determined the automaker’s Autopilot system was not to blame for a 2019 crash. In that case, the "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/04\/21\/tesla-wins-autopilot-crash-case-in-california\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">jury awarded no damages<\/a> to Los Angeles resident Justine Hsu, who sued Tesla in 2020 alleging negligence, fraud and breach of contract. The Molander v. Tesla case that wrapped up Tuesday was the first jury trial involving a fatality.<\/p>\n Tesla still faces a number of other lawsuits in California, including a wrongful death suit that was filed by the family of Walter Huang, an Apple engineer who died after his Tesla Model X with Autopilot engaged crashed into a highway median. The State of California Department of Transportation is also named in the lawsuit. That wrongful death lawsuit, filed in California Superior Court, County of Santa Clara, alleges that errors by Tesla\u2019s Autopilot driver assistance system caused the crash that killed Huang on March 23, 2018. Huang, who was 38, died when his 2017 Tesla Model X hit a highway barrier on Highway 101 in Mountain View, California. A jury trial is expected to begin next year in that case.<\/p>\n Tesla is also facing scrutiny from "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/08\/29\/nhtsa-raises-more-concerns-about-teslas-autopilot-safety\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">federal and state regulators,<\/a> all of which are related to Autopilot and its upgraded version known as Full Self-Driving.<\/p>\n Tesla vehicles come standard with a driver-assistance system branded as Autopilot. For a $6,000 upgrade, owners can purchase Enhanced Autopilot, which includes several other features, including an active guidance system that navigates a car from a highway on-ramp to off-ramp, including interchanges and making lane changes.<\/p> "piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n For an\u00a0additional $12,000, owners can buy \u201cfull self-driving,\u201d or FSD \u2014 a feature that CEO\u00a0 "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/elon-musk\/\" data-mrf-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/elon-musk\/\">Elon Musk<\/a>\u00a0has promised for years will one day deliver full autonomous driving capabilities.<\/p>\n Tesla vehicles\u00a0 "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/07\/tesla-refutes-elon-musks-timeline-on-full-self-driving\/\" data-mrf-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/07\/tesla-refutes-elon-musks-timeline-on-full-self-driving\/\">are not self-driving<\/a>. Instead, FSD includes a number of automated driving features that still require the driver to be ready to take control at all times. It includes everything in Enhanced Autopilot and is supposed to handle steering on city streets and recognize and react to traffic lights and stop signs.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" A jury on Tuesday handed Tesla another win after siding with the automaker over allegations that its Autopilot advanced driver assistance system led to a death. The case, which was being tried in the Superior Court of California, County of Riverside, was filed by two passengers who survived a 2019 crash and alleged that Tesla ","title":{"rendered":"So long, Twitter Circles"},"content":{"rendered":" "speakable-summary\">If tic-tac-toe has taught us anything, it’s that Xs and circles cannot peacefully coexist.<\/p>\n X, the app formerly known as Twitter, has shut down the Circles feature, which allowed users to post to a small, exclusive audience. Like an Instagram Close Friends story, Circles — n\u00e9e Twitter Circles — offered a more intimate social media experience. In other words, you could overshare about your life to an audience of friends only, rather than the whole internet. And isn’t one of the greatest joys of the internet to emotionally shitpost without worrying about the consequences?<\/p>\n But, as the whims of the Circle reminded us, nothing we say on the internet is ever actually free from consequence. The feature worked almost all of the time. Almost. And anything less than 100% efficacy is not ideal for a feature that people used to share private thoughts with trusted friends.<\/p>\n As early as February, some users reported that their Circle tweets were "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/02\/03\/twitter-circle-glitches-have-users-worried-about-privacy\/\">reaching a wider audience<\/a> than they were supposed to. These glitches showed up "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/04\/10\/twitter-circle-bug-not-private\/\">again in April<\/a>, and X (then known as Twitter) "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/05\/05\/twitter-confirms-circle-tweets-temporarily-were-not-private\/\">apologized<\/a> for the error in May, marking a rare moment of transparency for the company.<\/p>\n Even when Circle tweets were truly private, they often appeared not to be — the green banner denoting it as a Circle post only appeared some of the time (I had received some paranoid texts from friends who wondered if I knew I had posted about [redacted] on main, but nope, this was just the glitchy old bird app playing tricks on us).<\/p>\n "embed breakout embed-oembed embed--twitter\">\n "twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n "en\" dir=\"ltr\">I can't believe this website is going to take away my most treasured joke: my Twitter circle that only contains Tony Hawk.
"https:\/\/t.co\/P9pRF2HTIy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">pic.twitter.com\/P9pRF2HTIy<\/a><\/p>\n — Giovanni Colantonio (@MarioPrime) "https:\/\/twitter.com\/MarioPrime\/status\/1719398305526861961?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">October 31, 2023<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote> "piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n "https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n But perhaps nothing is sadder than the loss of "https:\/\/twitter.com\/MarioPrime\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">one user<\/a>‘s “most treasured joke,” in which he posted to a Circle audience consisting only of Tony Hawk, because you could add people who didn’t follow you to your Circle. And they could not remove themselves.<\/p>\n Some users have expressed concern that their private musings would be made public, now that Circles are no longer. So far, this doesn’t seem to be the case, though you’re able to view your own Circle tweets on your profile. But on X, who knows when something will break, so if you have anything salacious up, it might be worth deleting.<\/p>\n It’s not clear why "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/09\/21\/x-is-shutting-down-its-circle-feature-in-october\/\">X is sunsetting Circles<\/a> — perhaps it will come back as a paid benefit, like another beloved feature, "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/08\/15\/x-formerly-twitter-makes-x-pro-formerly-tweetdeck-a-subscriber-only-product\/\">TweetDeck<\/a> (now called X Pro). But users will understandably be annoyed if they have to pay money to X to regain features they used to have for free.<\/p>\n "embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n "wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"i0QNe6bERD\"> "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/04\/10\/twitter-circle-bug-not-private\/\">Twitter Circle tweets are not that private anymore<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n ndered":"SBF\u2019s defense puts forth a 35-minute last-ditch effort to show his goodwill"},"content":{"rendered":" "speakable-summary\"> "featured__span-first-words\">As Sam Bankman-Fried<\/span> took the stand for the last time in his trial for fraud and money laundering, his main lawyer, Mark Cohen, returned to question him on a number of themes that prosecutors touched on in the past few days. But this time, he took a different approach, presenting the defendant as a person who was acting in good faith.<\/p>\n \u201cWe lived and died by having a better product than competitors,\u201d Bankman-Fried said of his "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/11\/11\/ftx-files-for-bankruptcy-ceo-sam-bankman-fried-steps-down\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">now-bankrupt crypto exchange<\/a>, FTX. Bankman-Fried owned majority stakes in both FTX and its sister trading firm, Alameda Research, but insisted he wanted the best for both.<\/p>\n Bankman-Fried has been "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/26\/sam-bankman-fried-takes-the-stand\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">testifying since Thursday afternoon<\/a>, and the prosecution has grilled him for the past few days as "https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/30\/sam-bankman-fried-ftx-cross-examination\/\">part of their cross-examination<\/a>. On Tuesday, when the defense lawyers returned to reexamine him, he was swaying slightly on the stand, shoulders drawn down and forward. He spoke softly, but was more talkative than earlier in the day and on Monday when he was being questioned.<\/p>\n Contrary to the picture prosecutors tried to paint, Bankman-Fried insisted that he was not involved in the day-to-day trading operations of Alameda or its \u201ccore operations,\u201d but instead emphasized his concern for its leadership at the time, saying he wanted to be involved in many of its venture investments, decisions on hedging, and other areas.
